Post_ID: 2761202702763851797 | Post_Code: CZRwzqLFoAV | Likes: 123 | Time Stamp: 1643381034 | Tags: [] | Caption: Leave No Trace Principle 2: Travel and Camp on Durable Surfaces ⬇️<\br><\br>Continuing with our LNT series, let’s talk about principle 2!<\br><\br>Choosing durable surfaces to travel and camp on greatly impacts the degradation of the environment. <\br><\br>🥾RULE OF THUMB: stay on the provided trails. Trails are built to be able to limit the destruction of the nearby areas, to keep the traffic in a designated area. So, whenever possible, stay on the trail.<\br><\br>🥾BUT, LET’S BE REAL, there are times we have all gone off the trail! Whether you’re searching for a private “bathroom” area, taking a lunch break,  finding a campsite, or scrambling up some rock to get to a vista, it’s just part of hiking! <\br><\br>🪨 Because of this, it’s important to BE CONSCIOUS of where you travel off trail. Rocky areas are often able to withstand a lot more travel than vegetation and living soil. <\br><\br>👣 If you must travel through these areas, be conscious of your impact. (Sometimes this means spreading out from your group (vegetation), sometimes it means following exact footprints (soil))<\br><\br>🏕CAMPING on durable surfaces:<\br>Choose a campsite that either already has very high traffic (no vegetation left) or, in less trafficked areas, find locations you can have the least impact on. Generally, rock and sand are great areas to set up camp, as they will be able to withstand campers. <\br><\br>⛺️🥘CAMP COOKING: Set up camp kitchens on Rocky areas to avoid constant trampling on vegetation and soil. <\br><\br>This principle is EXTENSIVE and every situation differs. Your situation changes in different locations, the type of trip, and the local environment. We highly recommend you go check out lnt.org for more information on how to implement this principle, but we hope this gave you a good idea of the general guidelines!<\br><\br>Overall, it is our jobs to take into consideration the environment around us to decide how we can best limit our impact on each trip.<\br><\br>We also feel it’s important to recognize that while “stay on the trail” is a good rule of thumb, there are circumstances when you just CAN’T. Being able to know how to handle those moments and travel off trail responsibly is super important and can help us all to take better care of these lands!

Post_ID: 2760078930242506807 | Post_Code: CZNxSndJRA3 | Likes: 106 | Time Stamp: 1643247070 | Tags: ['#restoration', '#rangers', '#jmt', '#johnmuirtrail', '#wildernessrestoration', '#sustainable', '#camping', '#natural', '#naturalization', '#leavenotrace', '#lnt'] | Caption: Before and after - this is what campsite restoration looks like! <\br><\br>Picture 1 shows an illegal campsite that had been heavily used, leaving the area without vegetation or healthy soil. Post_ID: 2759941819536871849 | Post_Code: CZNSHZKPZGp | Likes: 24 | Time Stamp: 1643230725 | Tags: ['#WildernessWednesday', '#willdernessvolunteers', '#givingsomethingback', '#wildernesswednesdays', '#sangoroniowilderness', '#sangorgonio', '#sangorgoniopeak', '#sangorgoniopass', '#usfs', '#sanbernardinonationalforest', '#itsallyours', '#usforestservice', '#designatedwilderness', '#pacificcresttrail', '#pct', '#bureauoflandmanagement', '#blm', '#california', '#oldgraybackmountain', '#oldgrayback', '#optoutside', '#leavenotrace', '#lnt', '#photography', '#wilderness', '#camping', '#backpacking', '#colorpalette', '#colors', '#colorwheel'] | Caption: Happy #WildernessWednesday! Today we're taking in the beauty found in the San Gorgonio Wilderness in Southern California! Nestled in San Bernardino National Forest, this designated wilderness also resides within the Sand to Snow National Monument. <\br>.<\br>The San Gorgonio Wilderness consists of sub-alpine landscape surrounded by desert to the east, and covers 94,000+ acres. With elevations from 4,400'-11,500', you can experience soft rolling foothills, to canyons, to steep, impressive mountains. Due to the elevation gradient, this wilderness has a transition between desert, coastal and mountain environments, including the different types of vegetation representative of each elevation.<\br>.<\br>The U.S. Congress designated the San Gorgonio Wilderness in 1964, making it one of the first designated wilderness areas in the U.S. The wilderness is named after San Gorgonio Mountain, which at 11,499 ft. is the highest peak in California south of the Sierra Nevada. San Gorgonio Mountain, however, was originally known as "Old Grayback" by locals until officially designated by the US Geological Survey in 1899.<\br>.<\br>There are 81 miles of trails in the National Forest section of the Wilderness, and ~20 miles of the Pacific Crest National Scenic Trail in the Bureau of Land Management portion. <\br>.<\br>.<\br>.<\br>#willdernessvolunteers #givingsomethingback #wildernesswednesdays  #sangoroniowilderness #sangorgonio #sangorgoniopeak #sangorgoniopass #usfs #sanbernardinonationalforest #itsallyours #usforestservice #designatedwilderness #pacificcresttrail #pct #bureauoflandmanagement #blm #california #oldgraybackmountain #oldgrayback #optoutside #leavenotrace #lnt #photography #wilderness #camping #backpacking #colorpalette #colors #colorwheel

Sorghum syrup is similar to maple syrup or molasses, a sweet, sticky concoction derived form the sorghum plant. To make sorghum syrup, you crush the stalks of the sorghum plant, which produces a juice. The juice is then boiled, so that excess water evaporates as steam and only the sweet syrup remains.<\br>The Lyon family enslaved people prior to the Civil War, and continued to live on and farm the Lyon property until the early 2000's. This mill was used by later generations of the Lyon family as they worked on the farm. Post_ID: 2758599709314381047 | Post_Code: CZIg9HnLfT3 | Likes: 33 | Time Stamp: 1643070733 | Tags: ['#shetreks', '#wildernessmedicine', '#emergencypreparedness', '#backpacking', '#adventurecompany', '#womenwhobackpack', '#firstaid', '#planaheadandprepare', '#lnt', '#safetravels', '#nolswildernessmedicine', '#gossamergear'] | Caption: I spent the weekend renewing my Wilderness First Responder certification with @nolsedu 💉🩸<\br><\br>And it reminded me how much can go WRONG, especially in remote environments 🤕 <\br><\br>What gives me confidence, though, is the fact that planning ahead and preparing really DOES help prevent accidents. <\br><\br>And an ounce of prevention IS worth a pound of cure… <\br><\br>Here are some ways you can avoid catastrophe on your next trip into the backcountry: <\br><\br>👉 bring a first aid kit! The size/contents of your kit can fluctuate based on how many people are in your group, where you are traveling (remoteness) and for how long, and the activities you’ll be doing<\br><\br>👉 have a plan incase of emergency; who will you contact for help? Know how to deliver a detailed patient report to EMS/SAR in the event you need an evacuation, and make sure you have an exit strategy, even if it is just marching back out the way you came <\br><\br>👉 seek out first aid training! A WFA is more affordable but less comprehensive than a WFR, and a WEMT is the most comprehensive wilderness medicine cert you can obtain (check out @nolsedu for more course info)<\br><\br>👉 lastly, know your limits. If you plan to go BIG, do so with the understanding that you might have to bail, and make sure you CAN bail, some routes are more committing than others. <\br><\br>Anytime we go out into the backcountry, we do so knowing that there is some risk involved. And when (if) we call for help, we are asking others to put their lives on the line for us. <\br><\br>Traveling safely and sustainably in the backcountry is an intentional practice 🌱<\br><\br>Photo of Jai carrying the @gossamergear Mariposa, 📸 taken by @mountainmagicmedia <\br><\br>#shetreks #wildernessmedicine #emergencypreparedness #backpacking #adventurecompany #womenwhobackpack #firstaid #planaheadandprepare #lnt #safetravels #nolswildernessmedicine #gossamergear
